root.genUrl = function (routeName, context) {
        var route = routeMap[routeName],
            path, keys, i, len, key, param, regex;

        if (!route) { return ''; }

        path = route.path;
        keys = route.keys;

        if (context && (len = keys.length)) {
            for (i = 0; i < len; i += 1) {
                key   = keys[i];
                param = key.name || key;
                regex = new RegExp('[:*]' + param + '\\b');
                path  = path.replace(regex, context[param]);
            }
        }

        // Replace missing params with empty strings.
        return path.replace(/([:*])([\w\-]+)?/g, '');
    };

The premise was simple: When the ladies leave the house, the men just want to dance their hearts out. Dubbed an "instant classic by one  Entertainment Weekly commenter, the skit became a viral hit, the Twitter term #bdp started trending, and rave reviews poured in. The video was a hit on Yahoo, too: It became the most watched sketch from this season. Relive those amazing 3 minutes of twerking and hip shaking, and enjoy our most popular hits from this season of SNL, including the "Black Jeopardy" and Jonah Hill's run-in with Leonardo.

                                When host Tina Fey first took to the "Saturday Night Live" stage for the season 39 premiere, she brought company  the show's six new cast members: Beck Bennett, John Milhiser, Kyle Mooney, Mike O'Brien, Noel Wells, and Brooks Wheelan). And so the hazing began. Fey announced that their first job would be starring as her degraded backup dancers: "You'll be humiliated for the first time." Recalling her own checkered past -- prancing behind Jude Law and others in past seasons -- Fey lined up the newbies and issued the orders - including one for an embarrassing outfit change. "Remember, it was your dream to work here," Fey barks before demanding, "Bring it home, nerds!" The joke was on the freshmen again with the game show skit, "New Cast Member Or Arcade Fire?". More premiere highlights: "Breaking Bad" star Aaron Paul's three (!) cameos, a scathing parody of HBO's "Girls" with Fey playing stoic new Romanian roomie Blerta, and the old-time "Tin Lizzy" ad with Fey as a pitchman's decidedly uncooperative wife.

                              <div class="desc hidden" data-duration="3:35" data-pd="May 23, 2014">
                                Along with hit songs, serious dance moves, and killer looks, Beyonc also knows how to take a joke. To prove it, she posted her positive reaction to a "Saturday Night Live" sketch called "The Beygency.

So what did Queen Bey think of the satire? "Haaaaaaaaaaaa," the singer posted on Instagram, along with an image from the sketch.
In the standout skit, "SNL" guest host Andrew Garfield is chased down by "The Agency"-style operatives after he " he admits that one of the pop diva's songs "just doesn't do it for me.

On the run, Garfield stops at a convenience store, where he's told that his credit card has been declined. "They're erasing you. I know what you've done. Stay away from me!" yells the convenience store clerk, played by Bobby Moynihan. "But I like most of her music," Garfield responds.

In the next scene, in a shadowy parking garage, he's helped by "24" stars Kiefer Sutherland and Mary Lynn Raksub, where Sutherland reveals that he has also committed a crime against the Beygency: a Rihanna tattoo. Sutherland tells him everything he needs to escape is "to the left, to the left.  Still, hes caught, forced to do the "Single Ladies" hand wave, and thrown in jail.

We're glad Beyonc liked the sketch, because, in case she's reading this, we want her to know, we love everything she does. Really.

 Claudine Zap (@zapkidd)
                              </div>
                            </a>
                          </div>

                        <li data-uuid="d219f234-47c5-3f9c-8d6c-9e9e4f83f67a" data-provider-uuid="6b277d22-bbbb-3eba-b7a7-9ab5ba56fbd7" class="thumb hvr-info scrollstrip-item" data-idx="5">
                          <div class="img-wrap-16x9 view-count-item">
                            <a href="/snl/black-jeopardy-055848289.html" data-ylk="cat:SNL;g:d219f234-47c5-3f9c-8d6c-9e9e4f83f67a;pkgt:1;pub:6b277d22-bbbb-3eba-b7a7-9ab5ba56fbd7;sec:SNL;cpos:6;bpos:1;" class="rapid-nf">
                              <img src="https://s.yimg.com/os/mit/ape/m/81f43c2/t.gif" class="ImageLoader" style="background-image:url('https://s1.yimg.com/uu/api/res/1.2/C7unX9kpgMb1AVyCPamcFQ--/dz0yMDg7Zmk9ZmlsbDtweW9mZj0wO2g9MTE3O2FwcGlkPXl0YWNoeW9u/http://media.zenfs.com/en-US/video/video.snl.com/snl_1657_03_Black_Jeopardy.jpg')" alt=""/>
                              <div class="hover-overlay">
                              </div>
                              <div class="overlay">
                                <span class="Icon watch-later-button wl-icon" title="Add to Watch Later" data-action="add" data-action-str="Watch Later">
                                </span>
                                <p class="title">
                                  'Black Jeopardy'
                                </p>
                                <p class="view-count">
                                  946,500 views
                                </p>
                              </div>
                              <p class="show-name hidden">
                                Saturday Night Live
                              </p>
                              <p class="artist_name hidden">
                              </p>
                              <div class="desc hidden" data-duration="6:15" data-pd="Mar 30, 2014">
                                In this send-up of "Jeopardy," the twist is "Black Jeopardy," hosted by "Alex Treblack" (played by Kenan Thompson, who was also one of the writers of the sketch).

Louis C.K. plays the only white guy on the show and is clearly out of his element. He's "Mark," an African American studies professor who immediately realizes his mistake when instead of history, the category choices include "It's Been a Minute," "That Girl," and "Psssh!"

At one point, the professor jumps in to take the clue "It's been a minute since he got a job." His guess: "Who is unemployed fellow? Black?" He's met with scandalous looks from the other contestants, played by Jay Pharoah and Sasheer Zamata. "Wrong answer," he says.

The skit inspired lots of comments on the Web. Viewer Steven Melton (?@meltonstvn) raved on Twitter,
"The 'Black Jeopardy' skit on this weeks SNL was gold."

Former "Saturday Night Live" head writer Seth Myers (@SethMeyers) tweeted, "'Black Jeopardy' is just a wonderful piece of sketch writing."

The Wrap praised the sketch as "brilliantly irreverent."

Slate called out the moment as one of the highlights of the show's "absurdist and sometimes awkward sketches."

Self-mocking, odd, cringe-worthy: For Louis C.K. fans, that's a recipe for success.

This skit comes after "Saturday Night Live" faced criticism for its lack of cast diversity. Thompson stirred debate when he told TV Guide last year that the problem was finding qualified black female comedians. "Like in auditions, they just never find ones that are ready," he said. Following the backlash, the show hired Zamata along with two African-American writers.

--Claudine Zap (@zapkidd)

                        <li data-uuid="bc687fc4-8148-31ec-aa8f-57f054cf5188" data-provider-uuid="6588b68d-977e-3c5a-9fe5-d0054f6ec29d" class="thumb hvr-info scrollstrip-item" data-idx="6">
                          <div class="img-wrap-16x9 view-count-item">
                            <a href="/comedy-central/operation-deserter-storm-home-where-040000233.html" data-ylk="cat:Comedy Central;g:bc687fc4-8148-31ec-aa8f-57f054cf5188;pkgt:1;pub:6588b68d-977e-3c5a-9fe5-d0054f6ec29d;sec:Comedy Central;cpos:7;bpos:1;" class="rapid-nf">
                              <img src="https://s.yimg.com/os/mit/ape/m/81f43c2/t.gif" class="ImageLoader" style="background-image:url('https://s3.yimg.com/uu/api/res/1.2/H9udLqCB0hRPj8JuQPX2xg--/dz0yMDg7Zmk9ZmlsbDtweW9mZj0wO2g9MTE3O2FwcGlkPXl0YWNoeW9u/http://media.zenfs.com/en-US/video/video.comedycentral.viacom.com/06f85d32ff66164530024a097eaaa722')" alt=""/>
                              <div class="hover-overlay">
                              </div>
                              <div class="overlay">
                                <span class="Icon watch-later-button wl-icon" title="Add to Watch Later" data-action="add" data-action-str="Watch Later">
                                </span>
                                <p class="title">
                                  (Part 1) Operation Deserter Storm: Home Is Where the Hate Is
                                </p>
                                <p class="view-count">
                                  37,100 views
                                </p>
                              </div>
                              <p class="show-name hidden">
                                The Daily Show
                              </p>
                              <p class="artist_name hidden">
                              </p>
                              <div class="desc hidden" data-duration="4:57" data-pd="Jun 10, 2014">
                                How did Bowe Bergdahl go from being a prisoner of war to traitor in just over a week? On "The Daily Show" on Monday, Jon Stewart ripped into Fox Newss coverage of the Army sergeant, saying the network jumped to some hasty conclusions about Bergdahl's release. (Note: Some R-rated content appears at the end).
 

Stewart showed a series of Fox News clips that accused Bergdahl of being "anti-American," a "deserter or traitor or both," and, "in some respects as a kind of modern-day Lee Harvey Oswald."
  

So, to sum up: "In just a few days, this guy Bowe Bergdahl went from a guy who left base without permission to Muslim-terrorist-Kennedy-assassin," Stewart said.
  

Fox News has also taken aim at Bergdahl's bearded dad, Robert Bergdahl, who appeared at a Rose Garden ceremony with President Obama.
  

"Of course, the story of Bergdahl's traitorous terror conversion wouldn't be as credible if his father was not a high-ranking Taliban official," Stewart joked.
  

The "Daily Show" host mocked Bill O'Reilly of "The O'Reilly Factor" who suggested that Bergdahl's beard appeared Muslim. "I don't know, man, I get more of an Amish vibe off of that," Stewart said.
  

Steve Doocy of "Fox and Friends" questioned the advice Bergdahl's father reportedly gave his son to "obey his conscience." The Fox News co-host said that sounded like "Yeah, whatever you want to do, go ahead."
  

Stewart begged to differ.
  

"If someone says, 'Listen to your conscience,' they're not saying, 'Do whatever you want.' Your conscience is the opposite of the thing that tells you to do whatever you want to do. Your id is the thing that enables your darkest impulses. Your id. Think of it as the Fox News of your brain," he said.
  

To make the point, Stewart is then visited by his R-rated conscience, in the form of a potty-mouthed Jiminy Cricket. (Consider yourselves warned.)
 

 Claudine Zap (@zapkidd)

                            </a>
